### Photon Capital (@PhotonCap)
_Fri Jul 17 16:55:30 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 39 · ↻ 3 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/PhotonCap/status/2078161683923841073)

> Silicon cannot make light.
>
> You can build the modulators, waveguides, and detectors in silicon, but the light source still has to come from InP. So the more silicon photonics wins, the more InP sells. What looks like a materials war is a vertical division of labor.
>
> UMC and Tower both expanding 300mm on the same day just pulled that trade forward. The math is in the piece.
> $COHR $LITE $MTSI $AXTI

### Athu (@athuinvests)
_Fri Jul 17 19:16:58 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 75 · ↻ 3 · 💬 10 · [open on X](https://x.com/athuinvests/status/2078197286103113912)

> Portfolio up 45% YTD, down from the ATHs.
>
> The pullback has given me plenty of lessons that I’ll carry into the next leg up.
>
> A few I wanted to share:
>
> - Set a strict limit on % allocation to any single stock, even if conviction is 120%, mainly due to volatility and risks. Allocate more to less volatile or revenue-proven names. Big lesson on BALANCE.
>
> Example: $SIVE at 110 SEK felt fairly valued to me, and hitting my fair value range without trimming let it reach 40% of the portfolio. I’m still reflecting on that. As a 2027+ long, I stopped buying until 30 SEK recently. Would like a second opinion?
>
> - Know when to trim or add—not perfectly, since you can’t time the market—but having a process helps manage risk and allocate better (especially during bad sentiment periods like recently). Also keep more cash on hand. Big lesson on PATIENCE for me.
>
> Example: Could have added $AAOI lower than the $140–$150s. With $KXIAY, I could have added more slowly instead of all in during the dips (in terms of allocated capital). Lack of basic TA skills (which I’m building now) would have helped.
>
> That said, I remain heavily invested in the AI buildout and concentrated in a few sectors with stocks at 2x+ potential.
>
> That’s the risk I’m willing to take personally.
>
> Names:
> - Cloud: $NBIS, $BRUN
> - Compute/Packaging/Foundry: $INTC
> - Memory: $MU, $KXIAY, $MIRAE (Equipment/Test)
> - Photonics: $SIVE, $AAOI
>
> Decided that materials won’t be in my portfolio for now (no $AXTI, $SOI, etc.), unless I do swing trades. 👀 But still looking into an energy long. 😉
>
> In terms of diversification, I am opening up to another tech area like software/fintech or defense/space.
>
> Mag7? Not right now. Still young enough to take more risk.
>
> But again, tech or nothing! Mainly because I want to invest where I’m 120% convinced and understand the sector properly.

### Gaetano (@crux_capital_)
_Fri Jul 17 19:53:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 35 · ↻ 0 · 💬 5 · [open on X](https://x.com/crux_capital_/status/2078206352414110036)

> Alright, let's start with $VIAV
>
> Market cap: ~$9.2B
> Next-quarter guide: ~$432M (+6.2% QoQ, +48.7% YoY)
> Next-12M revenue: $1.80-1.95B, 32-43% growth
> Exit margins: 63-64.5% gross, 24-26% operating
>
> VIAVI sits in the test layer for the optical buildout
>
> They touch many different stages of testing
>
> > During lab and product development
> > During manufacturing and production
> > During installation, operating, and field management
>
> They have very broad exposure in the data center:
>
> > Traditional pluggables
> > LPO, LRO, NPO, CPO, XPO 
> > AECs 
> > Retimers
> > PCIe 
> > CXL 
> > Hollow Core Fiber
>
> So they can test the silicon-photonics component, the optical engine, the packaged module, the Ethernet system, the physical fiber network, and the live AI fabric.
>
> One thing that I really like is that complexity increases test intensity. CPO, NPO, and advanced packaging create more testing insertions per system, so they can grow from both higher network volumes and more test content attached to each build.
>
> Also their Network and Service Enablement (NSE) segment has gross margins above 65%, with management estimating that roughly 40–45 cents of each incremental revenue dollar can reach operating profit.
>
> Some risks: Spirent integration, weak cash conversion/dilution, multiple compression, and delays in 1.6T/CPO customer ramps.
>
> *Reported growth includes the acquired Spirent product lines, which contributed $54.2 million last quarter, so don’t treat all of that growth as organic.
> *Margins / Rev are my projections 
>
> NFA

> The bear circle jerk:
> - "AI is a bubble" - revenue doubling YoY, demand consuming every available wafer
> - "memory is a bubble" - HBM supply constrained with no relief until 2028
> - "photonics is a bubble" - optical chokepoints single-sourced, capacity sold out through 2029
> - "neoclouds get replaced" - $1B+ LTAs signed with new AI labs. Customer diversification strengthens the thesis.
> - "humanoids won't get anywhere" - factory deployment is real, not a demo
>
> Retail and bots scream "sell everything." The structural agreements keep getting signed - MU with QCOM, NBIS with Reflection AI. The buildout continues.
>
> The liquidation cascades through leverage, not thesis quality. Same pattern played out during tariff scares. The drawdown is a liquidity event, not a thesis break.
>
> Revenue inflection compounds in H2 2027. It's 2026. The thesis doesn't break because the calendar hasn't caught up.
>
> TLDR: the market is pricing liquidation velocity, not revenue trajectory. The separation when the leverage clears is the trade.
>
> what's the bear case here?

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HNdREnMbwAAzM_I.jpg

### P Equity Research 📰 (@pequityresearch)
_Fri Jul 17 21:10:41 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 130 · ↻ 14 · 💬 11 · [open on X](https://x.com/pequityresearch/status/2078225902027108605)

> Morgan Stanley: Optical vs Copper
>
> How do you think about the optical scale up opportunity in 2027, 2028, 2029, etc, and how does that relates to the Nvidia ecosystem and roadmap?
>
> A: We believe a small scale out adoption next year, with small volumes accounting for 10-15% penetration with scale out. We do think there are some low adoption with CPO until Feynman in 2029. Small, single digit adoption of CPO in 2028 and really scaling in 2029.
>
> You took your TAM to $73B, 4x from a year ago, talk about the drivers of that and how that compares to consensus and buy side out there?
>
> A: Driven by CapEx data points being 2x we were expecting last year, that is one vector of growth. The other is the cluster sizes being discussed are the biggest rivers of scale up network . We have gone from 8 to 72, then from a couple 100s to 1000s in the next couple generations. This acts as a multiplier to scale up multiplier.
>
> Talk about the exposure among Lumentum, Coherent, and Corning. Are there nuances between who is more exposed, less exposed?
>
> A: For CPO within scale out, it is generally positive for Lumentum. Doesn't necessarily changed a whole lot for Corning. With Coherent, they have to balance it out with transceiver business they have. For Lumentum it is the most positive because of the one customer they have on the transceiver side being google and they are not going to be adopting CPO. For CPO within scale up, it is opportunity for all 3. This is where copper gets replaced with fiber and lit up by lasers and optical engines made by Coherent an Lumentum. In terms of overall exposure, Lumentum has a bigger catalyst because of larger AI/DC revenue. It would be incremental for both Coherent and lumentum. Lumentum #1, Coherent or Corning #2.
>
> Tell me about the Corning Glass Bridge announcement that got the stock excited?
>
> A: This is not a new announcement. It was a paper they released in 2025 and a presentation they did that refocused the market on this technology. It is already part of the $10B photonics target the company discussed couple of months ago.
>
> In terms of catalyst for optical space, OCP (Open Compute Project) coming in October has gone popular. What are you expecting to hear from this?
>
> A: We think this will be a catalyst because it provides more exposure into hyperscaler behavior. OCP will give us a chance to see hyperscalers roadmap, it will focus on CPO, NPO adoption and the vendors involved.
>
> Copper is still the story for 2026 and 2027. We have seen this continued enthusiasm for ASICs. How is copper well positioned for this dynamic? Who are the well positioned beneficiaries?
>
> A: Copper life can be extended with use of retimers and better SerDes. Copper has a lot of runway before switching to optics. We will likely see a hybrid environment before going to 100% optics. A large debate in scale up is what fabric and protocol will become dominant other than NVLINK as we get into new XPUs and alternatives to Nvidia GPUs ramping. A big debate here is between UALink and ethernet. Ethernet is dependent on Broadcom's new ASICs ramping in 2H2027 into 2028, we think Broadcom will have opportunity to bundle XPU solutions with networking portfolio and are very well positioned in ethernet. On UALink, this is high optionality for Marvell and Astera Labs. Astera has the scale up switch for Trainium 3, this is a PCIe based solution. We think customers will want to move to UA Link eventually.
>
> You consider Keysight as an agnostic winner in R&D, regardless of the copper vs optical timeline. Explain your thesis and why do you see it pulling ahead?
>
> A: Keysight really ways in multiple ways when it comes to AI. First, it benefits from different types of architectures being discussed which all need to be tested with their equipment in labs. Second, when you move to higher speeds (400g laser vs 200g), it requires more complicated testing. Third, when architectures change frequently, like every 2 years, that boosts their business. The variety of architectures being tested matters.
>
> $ALAB $NVDA $AVGO $MRVL $CRDO $SMTC $APH $KEYS $COHR $LITE $GLW $GOOGL

> Through fiber. 
>
> Through optical transceivers. 
>
> Through routers. 
>
> Through radio networks smart enough to handle loads that didn’t exist three years ago.
>
> That infrastructure doesn’t build itself.
>
> And the company quietly sitting at the center of all of it, making the optical transceivers, the IP routers, the radio access networks, and now an AI native 6G platform launched not to long ago,  is a Finnish company that most people dismissed a decade ago and haven’t looked at seriously since.

>
> Nokia booked €1 billion in AI and cloud orders in a single quarter. JPMorgan just raised their target from $14 to $21. Nvidia invested $1 billion at $6.01 a share, a price the stock has since blown past. AI and cloud revenue grew 49% year over year last quarter. Optical networks up 20%. Operating profit beat estimates by 12%. Guidance raised. Network Infrastructure growth forecast doubled.
>
> Two days ago Nokia launched its AI RAN platform, a radio access network built natively for artificial intelligence that thinks and adapts in real time. Their CEO called it one of the most significant advancements in radio technology in decades.
>
> And Nokia makes their own indium phosphide lasers in house. In Pennsylvania. In a facility just expanded 10x. Every competitor buys their lasers. Nokia makes theirs. That distinction matters more every quarter as supply chain sovereignty becomes a national priority.
>
> Q2 earnings are July 23rd. Six days away. First report where the Nvidia partnership shows up in order books. First report where the Allentown photonics expansion starts contributing. First look at whether the €1 billion in Q1 optical orders is the floor or the ceiling.
>

>
> I believe $NOK Nokia is where it moves.

### P Equity Research 📰 (@pequityresearch)
_Fri Jul 17 22:17:49 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 114 · ↻ 22 · 💬 2 · [open on X](https://x.com/pequityresearch/status/2078242798571049071)

> Goldman Sachs: Innolight & Optical Modules
>
> Market Trends and Technology Migration
>
> > Speed Evolution: The industry is aggressively migrating toward higher-speed optical modules. 1.6T modules are moving toward volume production as the next mainstream standard, while 3.2T optical modules are expected to begin volume ramp-up in 2027.
>
> > Silicon Photonics (SiPh) Dominance: Silicon photonics is increasingly displacing traditional EML-based solutions due to lower power consumption, superior performance, and simplified packaging.
>
> > Penetration Rates: By 2026, SiPh penetration is projected to reach 60% for 800G, 80% for 1.6T, and 100% for 3.2T products.
>
> > Revenue Share: Silicon photonics' share of total optical module revenue is expected to surge from 28% in 2025 to 62% by 2028.
>
> Innolight Shipment and Market Share Highlights
>
> > Leadership: Innolight is the leading supplier of 1.6T pluggable modules. It is projected to hold a 50–60% market share of 1.6T modules in 2026. Other industry reports indicate Innolight's market share for 1.6T modules may reach as high as 50–70%.
>
> 1.6T and 3.2T Outlook:
>
> > 1.6T: Expected to become the "absolute mainstream" by 2027, with 45.72 million units projected to be shipped that year.
>
> > 3.2T: Following the ramp-up of 1.6T, 3.2T shipments are expected to double in 2028 compared to their initial volume ramp year in 2027.
>
> > Manufacturing & Capacity: To support this demand, Innolight planned a 155% year-on-year increase in capital expenditure for 2026 to expand production capacity.
>
> Market Dynamics: Volume, Revenue, and ASP
>
> > Speed Migration (Volume Mix): The market is shifting rapidly from legacy "Below 400G" speeds toward high-speed AI-focused modules. 
>
> While "Below 400G" accounted for 89% of shipment volume in 2025, that share is projected to decline to 77% by 2028E. 
>
> Conversely, high-speed modules are capturing significant volume: 1.6T modules are projected to grow from 1% of volume in 2025 to 10% by 2028E, and 3.2T modules are expected to reach 5% of total shipment volume by 2028E.
>
> > Average Selling Price (ASP) Trends: The report explicitly notes an assumed year-over-year (YoY) ASP decline for "like-for-like" products. 
>
> For example, the ASP for 1.6T modules is expected to drop from $840 in 2025 to $435 by 2028E. 
>
> The 3.2T module, which enters the market in 2027, has a high starting ASP of $1,023 in 2027E, which is then projected to decline to $768 by 2028E.
>
> Technological Shift: SiPh vs. EML
>
> > Silicon Photonics (SiPh) Adoption: The market is undergoing a significant transition from traditional EML-based materials to Silicon Photonics.
>
> SiPh revenue penetration is expected to increase from 28% in 2025 to 62% by 2028E.
>
> Correspondingly, the SiPh penetration rate (by volume) is projected to climb from 6% in 2025 to 18% by 2028E.
>
> Market Opportunity (TAM)
>
> > Total Addressable Market (TAM): The global optical module TAM is expected to grow from $34.2 billion in 2025 to a peak of $72.6 billion in 2027E, before moderating slightly to $69.1 billion in 2028E.
>
> > High-Speed Revenue Growth: The 1.6T and 3.2T segments represent the primary growth engines, with combined revenue for these categories projected to grow from $3.9 billion in 2025 to $44.9 billion in 2028E.

### mark (@cherryPayment)
_Fri Jul 17 22:38:17 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 8 · ↻ 0 · 💬 6 · [open on X](https://x.com/cherryPayment/status/2078247946894622934)

> 我认为是很合理的分析
>
> 首先我们需要知道底层逻辑为什么英飞拓可以作为行业晴雨表？
>
> 我们要知道英飞拓是全球最大光模块厂商之一，它的ASP走势和出货量确实能反映整个产业链的景气度。高盛这样的机构是不会无缘无故上调108%/119%的盈利预测，那么其背后一定有channel check支撑。
>
> 所以基于此我是倾向于把英飞拓理解为光子行业的”台积电”。
>
> 而这个逻辑是台积电的资本开支指引和产能扩张节奏，是整个半导体行业景气度的先行指标；同理，英飞拓的订单结构、ASP走势和产能规划，是光子产业链景气度的先行指标。当英飞拓的盈利预测被机构上修超过100%，这不仅仅是一家公司的好消息——这是整个生态的信号弹。
>
> 800G超预期这个信号很关键。800G目前仍是主力交付速率，超预期意味着数据中心扩建节奏比市场预期快，这对LITE这类以800G为主的厂商是直接利好。
>
> 1.6T/3.2T拉高ASP的逻辑也成立，更高速率产品单价更高，即使出货量不变，收入和毛利都会改善。
>
> 高盛预期英飞拓在硅光（Silicon Photonics）模块的出货量将显著超出此前预期。这背后是三个维度的需求同步爆发：
>
> •Scale Out（横向扩展）：更多GPU集群节点互联，需要更多光模块
>
> •Scale Up（纵向扩展）：单节点算力密度提升，对高速互联带宽需求更高
>
> •Scale Across（跨域扩展）：数据中心之间、城域网之间的互联需求增加
> 这三个维度的同步扩张，意味着光模块不再只是某一个场景的刚需，而是AI算力基础设施全面扩张的基础组件。
>
> 2. 1.6T/3.2T产品拉高ASP和利润率
> 光模块产品的迭代路径是：400G → 800G → 1.6T → 3.2T。更高速率的产品，单价更高，毛利率通常也更好。
> 1.6T和3.2T产品的加速渗透，意味着即使英飞拓的出货量增速放缓，其收入和毛利仍会因为产品结构升级而显著改善。这是一个量价齐升的逻辑——在AI Capex持续扩张的背景下，这个趋势有望延续至2028年。
>
> 3. AI Capex的持续扩张
>
> 微软、Google、Meta、亚马逊等全球四大超大规模云厂商的2025年资本开支指引，无一例外都在大幅提升。这些资金最终会流向哪里？算力芯片、服务器、网络互联设备——以及连接这一切的光模块。
>
> 英飞拓作为这条链条中最关键的环节之一，是AI Capex最直接的受益者之一。
>
> 所以我认为在方向正确 + 间接收益方面 ：我是倾向于 $soi 和 $sive的

### Investor Denis (@InvestorDenis)
_Fri Jul 17 23:05:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 20 · ↻ 5 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/InvestorDenis/status/2078254671198638361)

> Just found new evidence the US government is dead serious about developing quantum technologies.
>
> US research is funded partly through the National Science Foundation (NSF). If your grant application is approved, you receive money.
>
> The NSF launched an initiative called NSF X-Labs two months ago. The goal of the initiative is to fund teams of researchers, engineers, and entrepreneurs to solve specific scientific challenges.
>
> The funding available is $1,5 billion over the next decade.
>
> The first round of X-Labs couldn’t have been more explicit. It invited proposals on two topics:
>
> 1/ Scientific instrumentation for sensing and imaging (deadline for grant applications: July 13)
>
> 2/ Quantum systems: Interconnects and integrated photonics (deadline July 20)
>
> The initiative resonates with
>
> 1/ the $2 billion direct equity investment into nine quantum companies in May
>
> 2/ the Executive Orders on quantum in June that look to find companies capable of providing these technologies, e.g. $INFQ and $IONQ.
>
> It’s hard not to be bullish on a technology pushed by the US government.

### นักลงพุง (@naklongpoong)
_Fri Jul 17 23:32:05 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/naklongpoong/status/2078261485424304227)

> ตลาด Optical Module กำลังเข้าสู่ยุค 1.6T และ 3.2T พร้อมแรงหนุนจาก Silicon Photonics
>
> Goldman Sachs ระบุว่า อุตสาหกรรม Optical Module กำลังเร่งเปลี่ยนผ่านไปสู่โมดูลความเร็วสูงเพื่อรองรับการเติบโตของ AI Data Center โดย 1.6T กำลังก้าวขึ้นเป็นมาตรฐานหลักของตลาด ขณะที่ 3.2T จะเริ่มเข้าสู่การผลิตจำนวนมากในปี 2027
>
> การเปลี่ยนผ่านสู่ Optical Module ความเร็วสูง
>
> อุตสาหกรรมกำลังเร่งเปลี่ยนจากโมดูลรุ่นเดิมไปสู่ความเร็วที่สูงขึ้น
>
> 1.6T กำลังเข้าสู่การผลิตจำนวนมาก และจะกลายเป็นมาตรฐานหลักของตลาด
> 3.2T คาดว่าจะเริ่มผลิตในระดับ Mass Production ตั้งแต่ปี 2027
> Silicon Photonics กำลังแทนที่ EML
>
> Goldman Sachs มองว่า Silicon Photonics (SiPh) จะเข้ามาแทนเทคโนโลยี EML (Electro-Absorption Modulated Laser) อย่างต่อเนื่อง เนื่องจากมีข้อได้เปรียบหลายด้าน ได้แก่
>
> ใช้พลังงานต่ำกว่า
> ประสิทธิภาพสูงกว่า
> กระบวนการประกอบแพ็กเกจง่ายกว่า
>
> อัตราการใช้งาน SiPh ที่คาดการณ์
> 800G: 60% ภายในปี 2026
> 1.6T: 80%
> 3.2T: 100%
>
> ขณะที่สัดส่วนรายได้ของ Silicon Photonics จะเพิ่มจาก 28% ในปี 2025 เป็น 62% ภายในปี 2028
>
> Innolight ครองตลาด 1.6T
>
> Goldman Sachs ระบุว่า Innolight เป็นผู้นำตลาด Optical Module แบบ 1.6T Pluggable
>
> คาดว่าจะมีส่วนแบ่งตลาด 50–60% ในปี 2026
>
> ขณะที่รายงานจากแหล่งอื่นประเมินว่าส่วนแบ่งตลาดอาจสูงถึง 50–70%
>
> แนวโน้ม 1.6T และ 3.2T
>
> 1.6T
> คาดว่าจะกลายเป็นมาตรฐานหลักของอุตสาหกรรมภายในปี 2027
> ยอดจัดส่งปี 2027 คาดอยู่ที่ 45.72 ล้านโมดูล
>
> 3.2T
> หลังจาก 1.6T เริ่มแพร่หลายแล้ว
> ยอดจัดส่ง 3.2T ในปี 2028 คาดว่าจะเพิ่มขึ้นเป็น 2 เท่า ของปีแรกที่เริ่มผลิตในปี 2027
>
> เพื่อรองรับความต้องการดังกล่าว Innolight วางแผนเพิ่ม CapEx ปี 2026 ถึง 155% YoY เพื่อขยายกำลังการผลิต
>
> การเปลี่ยนแปลงของตลาดและ ASP
>
> ตลาดกำลังเปลี่ยนจาก Optical Module ความเร็วต่ำ ไปสู่ผลิตภัณฑ์สำหรับ AI อย่างรวดเร็ว
>
> สัดส่วนยอดจัดส่ง
> โมดูลต่ำกว่า 400G จะลดจาก 89% ในปี 2025 เหลือ 77% ในปี 2028
> 1.6T จะเพิ่มจาก 1% เป็น 10%
> 3.2T จะเพิ่มเป็น 5% ของยอดจัดส่งทั้งหมดภายในปี 2028
>
> ด้านราคาขายเฉลี่ย (ASP)
> Goldman Sachs คาดว่าราคาจะปรับลดลงตามการผลิตจำนวนมาก
>
> 1.6Tปี 2025: 840 ดอลลาร์
> ปี 2028: 435 ดอลลาร์
>
> 3.2Tปี 2027: 1,023 ดอลลาร์
> ปี 2028: 768 ดอลลาร์
>
> การเปลี่ยนผ่านจาก EML ไปสู่ SiPh
> ตลาดกำลังเปลี่ยนผ่านจาก EML ไปสู่ Silicon Photonics อย่างชัดเจน
> สัดส่วนรายได้ของ SiPh จะเพิ่มจาก 28% ในปี 2025 เป็น 62% ในปี 2028
> ส่วนแบ่งการใช้งานตามปริมาณ (Volume Penetration) จะเพิ่มจาก 6% เป็น 18% ในช่วงเวลาเดียวกัน
>
> โอกาสของตลาด (TAM)
>
> Goldman Sachs คาดว่ามูลค่าตลาด Optical Module ทั่วโลกจะเติบโตอย่างแข็งแกร่ง
> 2025: 34.2 พันล้านดอลลาร์
> 2027: 72.6 พันล้านดอลลาร์ (จุดสูงสุด)
> 2028: 69.1 พันล้านดอลลาร์
>
> ขณะที่รายได้จากกลุ่ม 1.6T และ 3.2T ซึ่งเป็นแรงขับเคลื่อนหลักของอุตสาหกรรม จะเพิ่มจาก
> 3.9 พันล้านดอลลาร์ในปี 2025
> เป็น 44.9 พันล้านดอลลาร์ในปี 2028

### P Equity Research 📰 (@pequityresearch)
_Fri Jul 17 23:48:55 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 61 · ↻ 7 · 💬 6 · [open on X](https://x.com/pequityresearch/status/2078265723747508264)

> Citi: EML Output
>
> > Industry Shift Toward 200G and CW: Across almost all listed companies, there is a marked transition away from 100G EML production by 2028, with a significant ramp-up in both 200G EML and CW output.
>
> > AXT, Inc. Growth: AXT, Inc. shows a substantial increase in its 200G EML and CW output, with its 200G EML output projected to grow from 13.54 million chips in 2025 to 157.82 million chips by 2028.
>
> > Rapid Expansion in China: Companies such as Source Photonics (Dongshan Precision) and the "Other China" category show dramatic growth in CW output. Source Photonics, for example, is projected to increase its CW output from 14.66 million chips in 2025 to 161.77 million chips by 2028.
>
> > Sumitomo Electric: Sumitomo maintains high production levels, particularly in the 200G EML segment, which jumps from 28.93 million in 2025 to 128.58 million in 2028.
>

### charahim94 (@charahim9494)
_Mon Jul 13 18:31:31 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 20 · ↻ 1 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/charahim9494/status/2076736294328365145)

> Over the years, co-packaged optics (#CPO) has been demonstrated with a variety of 💥light-source architectures, showing that there is no single universal approach. Some notable examples include:
> ✮IBM Power 775 (2010): one of the first commercial CPO implementations, using 850 nm VCSEL arrays
> ✮Hewlett Packard Enterprise’s 2 × 12.8 Tb/s switch demo (2012): also based on VCSELs but different wavelength than IBM (990nm?).
> ✮Rockley Photonics, Broadcom, Cisco, and Ayar Labs: using remote / external CW lasers
> ✮Intel: demonstrating integrated-laser with silicon photonics
> ✮RANOVUS Inc.: using a quantum-dot multi-wavelength laser platform, with both integrated and external-source variants
> ✮Avicena Tech LightBundle: using micro-LEDs, which are also relevant for CPO-style interconnect applications
> Each architecture brings different trade-offs in energy efficiency, reach, latency, cost per bit, and technology readiness.
> The table below summarizes the key attributes of the main light-source choices for CPO. It seems there is no one-size-fits-all answer. The right choice depends on reach, power budget, cost target, packaging approach, and manufacturing maturity.
> P.S: Is my collection of CPO implementations complete? Productive feedback is welcome❤️

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HNIMpj_WIAAOpmF.jpg

>
> That makes $SIVE interesting.
>

>
> Lasers are not the loudest part of the CPO story.

### Ahead (@AheadOfTmrw)
_Mon Jul 13 19:43:11 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 4 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/AheadOfTmrw/status/2076754329436905620)

> Interesting institutional validation for the $SIVE thesis.
>
> A Morgan Stanley report on co-packaged optics names Sivers alongside Lumentum and Coherent as a key laser supplier, while highlighting that CPO could reduce optical-interconnect power by roughly 50–80%.
>
> The report argues that value will increasingly shift toward suppliers controlling optical engines, silicon photonics, external lasers and advanced packaging.
>
> That is exactly where the Sivers opportunity sits. Silicon photonics still requires an external light source, making qualified InP laser suppliers strategically important as CPO scales.
>
> This is not a revenue confirmation, and Sivers still has to prove high-volume execution. But being included in the same institutional CPO supply-chain map as $NVDA, $AVGO, Ayar Labs, $TSM, $GFS, $LITE and $COHR is meaningful recognition for a company of its size.
>
> A ~$1.5B company named by Morgan Stanley alongside the two dominant Western laser players. Promising if i have to say so.

### Rosanna Prestia, MBA (@RosannaInvests)
_Mon Jul 13 20:03:18 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 760 · ↻ 81 · 💬 35 · [open on X](https://x.com/RosannaInvests/status/2076759395795665109)

> I mapped the entire future economy. Nine layers, from bedrock to orbit → and every layer is investable.
>
> 🛰️ SPACE → the orbital economy: $ASTS $RKLB $PL
> ⚡ ENERGY & STORAGE → powering the buildout: $TE $EOSE $SPKL
> 🚁 AUTONOMY & DRONES → machines that operate themselves: $ONDS $AUR $MRLN $KRKNF
> 🤖 PHYSICAL AI → intelligence that acts: $OUST $AMBA $OSS
> 💡 PHOTONICS → light replaces copper: $CRDO $SIVEF $AAOI $LITE 
> 🏗️ AI INFRASTRUCTURE → the compute buildout: $IREN $NBIS $DGXX $WYFI 
> 🔬 GLASS & OPTICAL MATERIALS → the substrate light runs on: $GLW $LPTH $LPKF
> 📡 CONNECTIVITY & RF → moving the signal: $AMPG
> ⛏️ CRITICAL MINERALS → the hard constraints under everything: $MP $UAMY $ASPI
>
> Here's what the map teaches that a watchlist can't: these aren't nine separate trades. They're one machine → the minerals feed the glass, the glass carries the light, the light feeds the compute, the compute powers the intelligence, the intelligence drives the machines, and the machines reach for orbit. Every layer is a chokepoint for the one above it.
>
> Which is the entire investing philosophy in one image: don't chase the logo at the top of the stack → own the layers everything above is FORCED to buy from. Logos compete. Layers collect.
>
> Important note: a map is a thesis, not a timing tool → layers de-rate together when the factor gets sold (see: this month), and not every name survives to see its layer win. Diversification across a stack is still one machine.
>
> The future economy isn't a sector. It's a supply chain → and it's hiring.

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HNIhPdxa4AAht3M.png

### Nirmātṛ (@En_formare)
_Mon Jul 13 21:17:37 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 4 · ↻ 0 · 💬 2 · [open on X](https://x.com/En_formare/status/2076778095147950241)

> Wavelength-scale nonlocal metadevices shatter finite-size Q limits, trapping light like an infinite crystal in a ring the size of a single wavelength while emitting pristine vector beams on demand. Researchers from Harbin Institute of Technology (Shenzhen), Pengcheng Laboratory, and collaborators fused bound states in the continuum (BICs) with topology to engineer nonlocal metasurfaces bent into closed, continuous-boundary rings. 
>
> Traditional finite nonlocal metasurfaces bleed radiation at edges, capping quality factors. Seamless loops eliminate lateral radiative channels, yielding experimental Q factors approaching 10^5 at true wavelength scales and rivaling ideal 1D infinite quasi-BICs. This topological approach conquers the boundary curse. 
>
> Strong meta-atom collective interactions suppress unwanted radiation while preserving controllable vertical emission. Multipole analysis shows the BIC mode dominated by magnetic dipole and electric quadrupole contributions, minimizing leakage unlike the leaky mode’s toroidal and quadrupole-heavy profile. Size-dependent tests confirm saturation at large radii matches the infinite-case limit, with robust fabrication tolerances against grating shifts, overlays, and height variations.
>
> Dual vector beam generation, radial and azimuthal polarizations, plus OAM beams and nonlinear responses from one compact device. On-chip photonics gains high-Q, mode-multiplexing capability for ultra-efficient light trapping in sensors, lasers, quantum tech, and structured-light applications, all in smaller-than-conventional footprints.
>
> Photonic chips can now confine light in whispering-gallery-like modes while emitting engineered vortices on cue, bridging classical confinement with nonlocal coherence. Like bending a leaky fence into an unbreakable Möbius loop, this seamless marriage of metasurface nonlocality and microcavity topology marks a record advance. Points toward scalable integrated photonics that defy size-Q trade-offs.

### Cal Conviction (@CalConviction)
_Mon Jul 13 22:01:34 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/CalConviction/status/2076789156349710633)

> $AEHR deep dive:
>
> Financials are ugly backward-looking, but interesting forward-looking. TTM revenue was USD 45.26M, TTM gross margin was 30.72%, free cash flow was negative USD 12.19M, and FY2027 consensus revenue was USD 85.14M, or about 71% growth.
>
> The thesis is that Aehr is becoming a tollbooth for testing the fragile stuff inside AI hardware: high-power AI ASICs, advanced packages, silicon photonics, and optical I/O. If these chips fail inside a data-center system, the customer has a very expensive bad day.
>
> The catalysts are real: Q3 FY2026 bookings were USD 37.2M, effective backlog was USD 50.9M, then Aehr announced a record USD 41M hyperscale AI package-level burn-in order. On June 17, it added a follow-on FOX-XP wafer-level burn-in system order from a major silicon-photonics customer, configured for nine wafers in parallel and scheduled for delivery within six months.
>
> The catch: the new SiPh order value and customer name were not disclosed, and the customer forecast for more systems this year is not backlog until purchase orders show up. At roughly USD 112, the stock was already around USD 3B-plus market cap, with stale analyst targets around USD 64. That is not exactly a bargain bin.
>
> Risks: valuation, customer concentration, bookings-to-revenue timing, gross margin recovery, and the classic small-cap semi equipment problem where everyone falls in love with the order headline before the revenue and margin proof arrives.
>
> Entry/Verdict: HOLD / catalyst watch / no add-size chase. Tiny tracker only if you want event exposure. Real add-size waits for FY2027 guidance above USD 100M-125M minimum, ideally toward USD 140M+, plus backlog conversion, margin recovery, and estimate revisions.
>
> The tech signal is real. The stock just needs the numbers to stop being theoretical. We'll see how it goes.

### Serenity (@aleabitoreddit)
_Mon Jul 13 23:17:46 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 933 · ↻ 41 · 💬 118 · [open on X](https://x.com/aleabitoreddit/status/2076808331453415674)

> TLDR of Innolight investor relations takeaways:
>
> 1. "Overall, 1.6T market demand has not contracted; instead, 800G demand has increased significantly compared with previous expectations"
>
> Prob most important takeaway as a whole was 800G demand revision (also longer tail demand). Which is a bullish read through on US transceiver makers like $AAOI, $COHR, $LITE. 
>
> Lot of new customers like neoclouds, AI model companies, contributing to overall demand rather than just hyperscalers, diversification always a bonus. 
>
> 2. Innolight said the shortage covers the module supply chain broadly including:
>
> - Optical chips.
> - Electrical chips.
> - PCBs.
> - Other module materials
>
> From last ER, I think they singled out EMLs and CW optical chips as the most constrained. So Innolight's bottleneck list mention broadened since then. 
>
> They expect some of the component availability to improve gradually from the second half of 2026 through the first half of 2027. 
>
> Think a lot of this is already known from earlier though. 
>
> But just some confirmation + easing timelines (EML is extremely bottlenecked, same with CW, this is probably talking about other components). 
>
> 3.  Innolight said module-production equipment is not the constraint. Equipment lead times remain relatively short. 
>
> So this isn't really a bottleneck compared to others. 
>
> 4. The overall proportion of silicon photonics continues to trend upward. Last year it was mainly 800G. This year, some 800G customers are further increasing their silicon-photonics proportion. 1.6T also added some new customers
>
> Positive for SiPH penetration eg. $SIVE / $JBL, since this shifts away from EML toward CW. 
>
> Basically: main surprising takeaway is just 800g demand go brrr. 
>
> Apart from that just reaffirming bottlenecks/timelines/market speculation.

### Stately (@116sbz)
_Mon Jul 13 23:35:50 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/116sbz/status/2076812877663719505)

> With the explosive growth of artificial intelligence, data centers are demanding increasingly higher computing power. 
>
> Traditional copper cables can no longer meet the extreme high-speed transmission needs of massive data, and they also generate excessive heat. Therefore, "optical communication" (using light instead of electricity to transmit data) has become the key to solving the computing bottleneck.
>
> In this sector, I believe three companies have the deepest "moats" (core competitive advantages) and the greatest future potential. 
>
> Here is a simplified, easy-to-understand breakdown:
>
> Lumentum (LITE): The "Profit Harvester" 
>
> Mastering Core Physics
> Lumentum's core advantage lies in its extremely high "technical barriers" and overwhelming pricing power. Simply put, as tech giants demand increasingly faster optical transmission speeds, it becomes incredibly difficult to manufacture lasers that can work stably at high temperatures while maintaining extremely pure light sources. Lumentum has successfully conquered this physics problem, producing top-tier 200G lasers. Because the technical threshold is so high—competitors either can't make them or can't make them well—Lumentum can sell its products at prices far above the industry average, causing its profit margins to soar. Furthermore, NVIDIA recently invested a massive $2 billion to lock in Lumentum's future production capacity. This means their current situation is one where demand far outstrips supply, and their only worry is manufacturing fast enough.
>
> Coherent (COHR): The "Industry Tollbooth" 
>
> Controlling Core Materials
> If Lumentum wins on the extremely high profit margins of individual products, Coherent's moat is built on "absolute production scale" and "scarce manufacturing capabilities." Currently, the biggest bottleneck in the entire optical communication industry is a shortage of a critical material called Indium Phosphide (InP). Coherent is upgrading its production from traditional smaller wafers to larger 6-inch wafers. This upgrade allows them to produce four times as many devices at once while cutting the cost per device in half. What's most impressive is that they handle everything themselves, from the foundational materials to the final finished products, without relying on others. Also having received a $2 billion investment from NVIDIA, Coherent is transforming from a standard hardware supplier into a foundational "tollbooth" that all AI data center builds cannot bypass. While they are currently spending a lot of money to build out factories, in the long run, this scale advantage will be very difficult for competitors to overcome.
>
> Marvell (MRVL): The "Chip Design Pioneer" 
>
> Leading Next-Gen Architecture
> Marvell's advantage lies in its powerful "ecosystem and chip design capabilities." Unlike the first two companies that build their own factories to manufacture hardware, Marvell focuses on the design of silicon photonics technology and custom networking chips (leaving the actual production to foundries). The future trend is that optical communication equipment will be increasingly and deeply integrated directly with computing chips, and Marvell stands right at the center of this technological architecture shift. They have already successfully shipped over 5 million complex photonic integrated circuits (PICs), proving their strong ability to execute and deliver technology. Marvell has the fiercest upward momentum among these three companies and is the purest play on the combination of custom chips and optical networks. However, it is important to note that precisely because everyone is so optimistic about it, its current stock price (valuation) is already very high, making it a choice where high risk and high reward coexist.
>
> Technical Support of these stock at 200EMA:
>
> $LITE SUPPORT AT 600
> $COHR SUPPORT AT 260
> $MRVL SUPPORT AT 150

This business has become one of Soitec's fastest-growing segments.

>

>
> As hyperscalers deploy larger AI clusters, demand is accelerating for silicon photonics, co-packaged optics (CPO), and high-bandwidth optical transceivers—all areas where Soitec has established technological leadership.
>
> Institutions aren't valuing Soitec as a traditional wafer supplier.
>

### john jacket (@jacket82488)
_Sat Jul 11 14:32:21 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/jacket82488/status/2075951330305474659)

> 【半導体・AIインフラの地殻変動】 「AIの限界はソフトではなく物理（電力と信号）にある」
> 現在、AIクラスターが直面している「電力」と「光・信号」の圧倒的な物理的ボトルネック、そしてその裏で覇権を握る黒幕企業について、Techトレンドをまとめました。
>
> 半導体投資やインフラに関わる人は【ブックマーク】推奨です🧵👇
>
> ⚡ 電力のボトルネック：アナログの逆襲と物理の限界
>
> アナログ半導体の時代到来：ムーアの法則が適用されないアナログ領域の価値が爆発中。TI、NXP、Infineon等の主要ベンダーは2026年に一斉値上げを断行。供給側が圧倒的な価格決定権を持つ市場へシフトしている。
> 12,500Aと800V直流の物理的限界：600kW〜1MW級の超高密度AIラックで従来の48V給電を続けると、電流は12,500Aに激増し熱損失で崩壊する。電流を750Aに抑え、銅材を45%削減できる「800V架構」への移行は物理的な必然。
>
> VPD（垂直電力給電）：GPUコア（約0.7V）への降圧時の損失を防ぐため、電源変換器をGPUチップの「真下」に配置するVPD（電源界のCPO）が急速に台頭。
> 📡 信号・光学のボトルネック：銅の延命と光の現実
>
> 「光が銅を完全駆逐」は誤り：実際は距離に応じた住み分け。短距離（Scale-up領域）は銅線とアナログコンポーネントが粘り、長距離（ラック間接続）を光が担う。
> Semtechのアナログ・マジック：200G/laneの超高速通信において、消費電力と遅延の元凶であるDSPを完全に排除し、アナログイコライザのみで信号を補正するSemtechの技術が激アツ。消費電力を10分の1に、遅延をns（ナノ秒）からps（ピコ秒）へと一気に縮小。
>
> 真のボトルネックは「光源」にあり：長期的な正解はCPOだが、今後2〜3年の現実的な勝者はNPOや1.6T可挿入型モジュール。本当のボトルネックはさらに下流の、InP（インジウムリン）基板、CWレーザー光源、Soitecが独占するPhotonics-SOIウェハ、そしてシリコンフォトニクス（SiPho）ファウンドリにある。
> 網 ネットワーク信頼性と「Link Flap」の恐怖
>
> Link Flap現象がすべてを止める：光リンクが一瞬だけ瞬断する「Link Flap」が発生すると、AIクラスター全体の同期演算（all-reduce）が中断され、膨大なGPUが完全なアイドル状態（サボり）になる。
> 帯域よりも信頼性の時代へ：超巨大クラスターにおいて、単に帯域を広げるだけでなく、この瞬断を絶対に起こさない信頼性を保証できるソリューション（Credoの『Zero-Flap』など）が、AIビジネスの経済性を左右する最終ボトルネックになっている。
>
> 💡 まとめAIの進化は、最先端の1nm/2nmプロセスだけでなく、それを支える「電源（VPD/800V）」や「アナログ信号処理（Semtech等）」、「光源のサプライチェーン（Soitec等）」にいかに強みを持つかで勝負が決まるフェーズに入っています。
> #生成AI #半導体 #NVDA #株クラ #テクノロジー

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HM9CujybEAAYGTJ.jpg

### TickerTalks (@TickerTalksX)

> Before a chip ships, it gets "burned in": baked under heat and voltage for hours so the ones destined to fail early die on the test bench, not in the field.
>
> $AEHR (Aehr Test Systems) builds the machines that do this at the wafer level. It grew up testing the silicon carbide chips in EVs.
>
> On July 9 its lead silicon photonics customer placed a follow-on production order for those systems, to burn in the optical transceivers that shuttle data between chips inside AI data centers.
>
> Same testing step, now moving from EV power into the optical layer of the AI buildout. The stock has more than tripled in the past year. Fiscal Q4 numbers land July 14.

### ᜱ𐤠㇜I ⵉ ᜤ 👽 ᜱ । ⚡︎ । ⚛ ᜤ (@ValienVision)
_Sat Jul 11 16:11:28 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/ValienVision/status/2075976273768137041)

> Physical AI pick-and-shovel ⌁ $NOVT DD  🔖🛸
>
> I spend a loooot of time evaluating the physical AI stack... with perhaps a slightly greater focus on humanoids.
>
> Software models are expanding at an extraordinary pace, yet the immediate scaling constraint remains entirely hardware-bound.
>
> Advanced whole-body control policies require instant, flawless translation into the physical world. 
> It starts with perception, flows through planning and control, then reaches the physical world through motion, force feedback and actuation.
>
> Every stage compounds error, so micro-second precision and adaptive force feedback determine whether an AI brain can function in reality or fail during contact-rich tasks.
>
> The sim2real gap is a hardware execution problem... 
>
> That's why I keep coming back to Novanta.
>
> The company has built an ecosystem that occupies the exact center of this hardware constraint. 
> They deliberately focus on manufacturing the core precision motion, sensing, and also photonics stacks that advanced robotics OEMs require.
>
> 🛸 ⌁ Motion stack
> Precision motion from Celera Motion and Ingenia supplies the encoders (Aura series and IncOder CORE), frameless and slotless high-torque motors (Omni+ line), and certified servo drives (Denali and Everest Safe equipped with FSoE).
>
> The result is (custom) actuators with sub-micron feedback and cogging-free smoothness paired with deterministic real-time control loops needed for stable locomotion and fluid multi-DOF manipulation. 
>
> 🛸 ⌁ Sensing stack
> ATI Industrial Automation (one of their greatest acquisition) contributes multi-axis force/torque sensors from the Axia and Varo families together with automatic tool changers and material removal tools that turn position-controlled arms into systems capable of compliant grasping, adaptive manipulation, and importantly safe human interaction. 
>
> These components matter for collision detection in unstructured environments and for force-modulated actions where pure kinematic control falls short.
>
> 🛸 ⌁ Photonics stack
> The photonics capabilities, built around Cambridge Technology beam steering, Synrad CO2 sources, Laser Quantum solid-state and ultrafast lasers, plus ARGES scanning, support high-precision material processing. 
>
> That matters both for manufacturing the next generation of robots and for the AI-optimized production cells those robots will eventually run inside factories and warehouses.
>
> The laser sources, beam steering, scan heads, and related photonics technologies supplied by Novanta are also used in medical laser procedures, such as ophthalmology, dermatology/plastic surgery, soft tissue applications, and support for minimally invasive/robotic surgery systems.
>
> 🛸 ⌁ Healthcare stack (robotics surgery)
> Continuing on the medical side, WOM insufflators, NDS visualization systems, but also integrated motion solutions underpin minimally invasive and robotic procedures. 
>
> Riverpoint brings high-growth minimally invasive surgical consumables (like advanced surgical fibers, sutures, and implants for trauma and cardiovascular applications).
>
> As AI moves into semi-autonomous subtasks in surgery to autonomous surgery, the same precision motion and force sensing that serve humanoids translate directly into safer, more consistent tissue interaction and better visualization pipelines, and vice-versa. 
>
> 🛸 ⌁ Final thoughts
> What stands out is how the pieces fit together.
>
> Acquisitions stitched a full motion and sensing stack, with end-effector tooling and supporting photonics into one offering. 
>
> That integration reduces risk for OEMs who must hit safety and reliability thresholds for real-world deployments. 
>
> Physical AI patform builders still do the system integration and higher-level control. Novanta supplies the subsystems that let those platforms actually perform at the edge of what physics allows.
>

### Yunis Rzayev (@rzayev7895)
_Sat Jul 11 18:38:31 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 73 · ↻ 1 · 💬 5 · [open on X](https://x.com/rzayev7895/status/2076013282071306423)

> KULICKE & SOFFA INDUSTRIES, INC. ( $KLIC)
>
> Kapsamlı Şirket Değerleme ve Stratejik Analiz 
>
> 1. Yönetici Özeti ve Stratejik Yol Ayrımı
>
> Yarı iletken endüstrisinde Moore Kanunu'nun fiziksel sınırlara dayanması ve ön uç (front-end) litografi maliyetlerinin katlanarak artması, performans artışının yeni odağını İleri Seviye Paketleme  ve Heterojen Entegrrasyon süreçlerine kaydırmıştır. Kulicke & Soffa, tarihsel olarak otomotiv, endüstriyel ve tüketici elektroniğine hitap eden olgun tel bağlama pazarında %80’e yakın pazar payıyla ezici bir cash cow yönetmektedir. Ancak şirket, son iki yıldır akademik ve kurumsal analizlere konu olan (örneğin 2025 sonundaki Harvard Business School stratejik vaka analizindeki gibi) çok kritik bir yol ayrımındadır: Olgun pazarlardaki nakit akışını koruyarak, yapay zeka (AI) ve yüksek performanslı bilgi işlem (HPC) çiplerinin mimarisini belirleyen ileri seviye montaj teknolojilerine liderlik etmek.
>
> FY2026 ikinci çeyrek sonuçları ve güncel pazar dinamikleri, KLIC’in bu teknolojik dönüşümü başarıyla gerçekleştirdiğini ve döngüsel bir dipten çıkış (cyclical inflection) dönemine girdiğini doğrulamaktadır. Şirket, karlılığı düşük olan Electronics Assembly iş kolunu tamamen kapatarak odağını netleştirmiş, yapay zeka veri merkezlerindeki bant genişliği kısıtlamalarını çözen Thermo-Compression Bonding ve Silicon Photonics çözümlerinde vites artırmıştır.
>
> 2. Finansal Performans ve Döngüsel Kaldıraç Analizi
>
> KLIC’in finansal yapısı, arka uç (back-end) sermaye ekipmanı üreticilerinde görülen yüksek operasyonel kaldıraç karakteristiğini taşımaktadır. Sektörel envanter düzeltmelerinin sona ermesiyle birlikte, gelir artışı marjlar üzerinde çarpan etkisi yaratmaktadır.
>
> Çeyreklik Finansal Gerçekleşmeler ve Dinamikler
>
> -- Gelir İvmesi: Q2 FY2026 net geliri, bir önceki çeyreğe göre %21.5, geçen yılın aynı dönemine göre ise %49.8 artarak 242.6 milyon USD seviyesine ulaşmıştır. Bu rakam, konsensüs beklentisi olan 191.4 milyon USD’yi büyük bir sürprizle geride bırakmıştır.
>
> -- Brüt Kar Marjı Genişlemesi: Brüt marj %49.3 olarak gerçekleşmiştir. Geçen yılın aynı çeyreğindeki %24.9'luk seviyeye kıyasla 2,440 baz puanlık operasyonel genişleme, yüksek marjlı Advanced Solutions ve bellek ürün miksinin devreye girmesiyle açıklanmaktadır.
>
> -- Karlılığa Dönüş: GAAP operasyonel karı 38.5 milyon USD'ye yükselmiştir. Geçen yılın aynı döneminde kaydedilen ağır zararların ardından, Non-GAAP operasyonel kar marjı %19.1’e (46.3 milyon USD) fırlamıştır. Non-GAAP EPS ise 0.79 USD ile beklentilerin 0.12 USD üzerinde gelmiştir.
>
> Q3 ve Q4 FY2026 Öngörüleri
>
> Şirketin resmi Q3 FY2026 kılavuzu, ardışık olarak %28 büyüme ile 310 milyon USD gelir hedeflemektedir. Operasyonel giderlerin (OpEx) 85 milyon USD seviyesine çıkması, üretim hacmini (production ramp) desteklemek için yapılan mühendislik istihdamları ve değişken performans primlerinden kaynaklanmaktadır. Yönetim, Q4 FY2026 döneminde de Q3'e kıyasla %5 ile %10 arasında organik bir büyüme trendinin korunacağını öngörmektedir. Bu doğrultuda FY2026 toplam geliri yaklaşık 1.07 milyar USD bandına doğru ilerlemektedir.
>
> 3. Segment Bazında Operasyonel ve Teknolojik Derinleşme
>
> KLIC’in ürün portföyü, yarı iletken dünyasının hem olgun hem de en uç teknolojilerine eş zamanlı hizmet verecek şekilde yeniden yapılandırılmıştır.
>
> -- Olgun Pazarlar: Ball/Wedge Bonding ──> Nakit Üretimi & Hacim (Akıllı Telefon, Otomotiv, Endüstriyel)
>
> -- Seküler Pazarlar: Advanced Solutions ──> TCB, FTC, ProMEM Suite, Vertical Wire (AI, HPC, HBM)
>
> -- İstikrar Segmenti: APS ──> Fabrika Kullanım Oranlarına Bağlı Yedek Parça ve Servis Güvencesi
>
> A. Geleneksel ve Hafif Döngüsel Segmentler
>
> -- Ball Bonding Equipment (Tarihsel Pay: %44.8): Klasik altın ve bakır tel bağlama sistemleridir. Akıllı telefon, PC ve alt segment tüketici elektroniğindeki döngüsel toparlanma, bu segmenti Q2 FY2026'da yeniden ana gelir sürücülerinden biri haline getirmiştir (GenSemi gelirleri çeyreklik %19.4 artışla 148.9 milyon USD olmuştur).
>
> -- Wedge Bonding Equipment (Tarihsel Pay: %16.9): Güç yarı iletkenleri, elektrikli araç (EV) batarya paketleri ve endüstriyel modüllere hizmet eder. Otomotiv sektöründeki elektrifikasyon trendiyle daha stabil bir grafik çizmektedir.
>
> -- Aftermarket Products & Services (APS) (Tarihsel Pay: %23.9): Küresel kurulu makine parkının sarf malzemeleri ve servis hizmetleridir. Donanım satışları düşse dahi, fabrikaların çalışmasına paralel olarak sürekli nakit üreten, döngüselliği en düşük defansif kalkandır.
>
> B. Yeni Nesil Hafıza (Memory) ve Güç Çözümleri (2026 İnovasyonları)
>
> Bellek segmenti, kurumsal SSD (eSSD) ve yüksek performanslı sunucu talebiyle Q2 FY2026'da çeyreklik bazda %93 büyüme kaydederek 31.3 milyon USD'ye ulaşmıştır. Şirket bu ivmeyi kalıcı kılmak adına Mart 2026'da iki büyük teknolojik silahını duyurmuştur:
>
> 1. ProMEM Suite: Standart yüksek hacimli bellek montajında (Stacked NAND) üretkenliği ve proses kontrolünü dramatik şekilde artıran bir ball bonding yazılım ve donanım paketidir.
>
> 2. Vertical Wire Teknolojisi (ATP MEM PLUS): Geleneksel tel bağlamayı dikey boyuta taşıyarak ara bağlantı yoğunluğunu artırır ve paket ayak izini küçültür. Stacked DRAM ve yeni nesil yüksek yoğunluklu bellek mimarilerinde silikon delikli geçişlere (TSV) karşı son derece maliyet etkin bir alternatif sunmaktadır.
>
> 4. Gelişmiş Paketleme ve AI Altyapı Katalizörü
>
> Advanced Solutions segmenti altındaki Thermo-Compression Bonding (TCB), KLIC'in uzun vadeli seküler büyüme motorudur. Şirket, TCB iş kolunun FY2026’da çeyreklik bazda en az %70 büyüyeceğini ve tek başına 100 milyon USD+ barajını aşacağını doğrulamıştır.
>
> Fluxless TCB (FTC) ve Teknik Üstünlük
>
> Gelişmiş veri merkezi işlemcilerinde kullanılan alt bileşenlerin kalınlıkları azaldıkça ve kalıp boyutları büyüdükçe (30 mm ve üzeri), geleneksel "flip-chip" yöntemleri termal eğrilme ve hizalama hatalarına neden olmaktadır. KLIC’in Fluxless TCB (FTC) teknolojisi bu problemi şu inovasyonlarla çözmektedir:
>
> -- Mikron Altı Hassasiyet: Lehim tabanlı bağlantıları 10 μm hatveye (pitch), doğrudan bakır-bakır bağlantıları ise en az 5 μm hatveye kadar indirebilmektedir.
>
> -- Formik Asit Buharı Oksit İndirgeme: Süreç esnasında sıvı akı (flux) kullanılmadığı için kalıplar arasında neredeyse "sıfır boşluk yüksekliği" elde edilir; bu da elektriksel direnci düşürür ve termal yönetimi optimize eder.
>
> -- Co-Packaged Optics ve Silikon Fotonik: Yapay zeka kümelerindeki anahtarlama ve ağ hızlarını artırmak için optik transceiver bileşenlerinin doğrudan işlemci yanına TCB ile montajlanması sürecinde KLIC, küresel lider dökümhanelerden ve OSAT'lardan peş peşe siparişler almaktadır.
>
> 5. Kapasite Genişletme ve Gelecek Projeksiyonları
>
> Advanced Solutions segmentinin ölçeklenebilmesi için üretim darboğazlarının aşılması gerekmektedir. Şirket yönetimi bu doğrultuda stratejik bir sermaye hamlesi yapmıştır:
>
> 1. CapEx Artırımı
> CapEx Artırımı:FY2026 Dönemi.Şirket, yıllık sermaye harcaması (CapEx) bütçesini 12 milyon USD seviyesinden 22 milyon USD seviyesine neredeyse iki katına çıkarmıştır.
>
> 2. Üretim Hatlarının Modernizasyonu:
> Q3/Q4 FY2026. Artırılan bütçe doğrudan Singapur ve ilgili üretim tesislerinde Fluxless TCB ve dikey tel montaj hatlarının otomasyon kalitesini yükseltmek için kullanılmaktadır.
>
> 3.Kapasite Hedefine Ulaşılması:
> Erken FY2027. Yapılan bu yatırımlarla Advanced Solutions segmentinin yıllık üretim ve sevkiyat kapasitesi run-rate bazında 400 milyon USD satış potansiyeline ulaştırılacaktır.
>
> Sipariş birikimini gösteren backlog yapısı da bu süreci desteklemektedir ve hızla artmakdadır. Siparişlerin iptal edilebilir olması bir risk olsa da Çin, Tayvan ve Kore'deki fabrika kullanım oranlarının %90'ın üzerinde seyretmesi, bu siparişlerin büyük ölçüde realizasyonla sonuçlanacağını göstermektedir.
>
> 6. Sektörel Karşılaştırma ve İleri Dönük Değerleme Modeli
>
> Yarı iletken ekipman pazarında değerleme yapılırken ön uç (ASML, KLA, Lam Research, Applied Materials) ve arka uç (KLIC, Besi, ASMPT) ayrımı kritik rol oynar. Ön uç firmaları daha az döngüsel ve yüksek bariyerli oldukları için tarihsel olarak yüksek çarpanlara sahiptir.
>
> KLIC ise tarihsel olarak olgun wire bonder pazarının dalgalanmalarına maruz kaldığı için düşük çarpanla işlem görmüştür. Fakat Advanced Solutions segmentinin kapasitesinin 400 milyon USD'ye ayarlanması ve TCB'nin yüksek karlılığı, çarpan genişlemesini tetiklemektedir.
>
> Akran Grubu Karşılaştırma Analizi (FOTO - 1)
>
> 2027 Gelir ve Çarpan Projeksiyonu
>
> -- FY2026 Tahmini Gelir: ~1.07 milyar USD (Mevcut çeyreklik gidişat ve Q3 kılavuzu tabanlı).
>
> -- FY2027 Projeksiyon Geliri: Bellek toparlanması, ProMEM Suite adaptasyonu ve TCB'nin yıllık 100 milyon USD'lik barajı kırıp Advanced Solutions run-rate'ini yukarı taşımasıyla 1.25 milyar USD (%17-20 civarı bir yıllık büyüme).
>
> -- Değerleme Yaklaşımı: Advanced Packaging payının artması sebebiyle şirkete hak ettiği tarihsel iskontonun üzerinde, 6x Forward P/S (İleri Dönük Satış) çarpanı uygulanması rasyoneldir. Bu çarpan altında şirketin adil kurumsal değeri 7.5 milyar USD olarak hesaplanmaktadır.
>
> Şirketin kasasındaki 254.3 milyon USD net nakit ve sıfır borç yapısı, hisse başına değer hesaplamasında ekstra bir emniyet marjı sunmaktadır. Finansal modelleme kapsamında %8 iskonto oranı tatbik edildiğinde, hisse senedinin önümüzdeki 12 aylık periyotta 135 USD adil değer hedefine doğru re-rate edilmesi beklenmektedir. Bu da mevcut konsolide fiyata göre yaklaşık %20 yukarı potansiyel anlamına gelir.
>
> 7. Derinlemesine Risk ve Tehdit Analizi
>
> Risk Matrisi ve Stratejik Tehditler: KLIC pozisyonlanmasında aşağı yönlü risklerin yakından izlenmesi gerekmektedir.
>
> I. İkame Teknolojiler ve Hibrit Bağlama Tehdidi
>
> En uç seviye AI hızlandırıcılarında (NVIDIA, AMD vb. yeni nesil mimarileri) TCB hatvelerinin dahi yetersiz kaldığı noktalarda Hybrid Bonding (Doğrudan Bakır-Bakır Die-to-Wafer entegrasyonu) devreye girmektedir. Bu alanda Hollandalı BE Semiconductor (Besi) tartışmasız pazar lideridir ve ana dökümhanelerin (TSMC vb.) onaylı tedarikçisidir.
>
> Risk: Eğer Hybrid Bonding teknolojisi beklenenden daha hızlı ucuzlar ve orta segment çiplere de hızla adapte edilirse, KLIC'in TCB pazarı daralabilir. KLIC, 2024'ten bu yana kendi bünyesindeki Hibrit Bağlama AR-GE programını hızlandırdığını ve erken müşteri test aşamasında olduğunu (Mart 2026 güncellemelerinde) belirtse de Besi ile olan teknolojik ve zamansal makası kapatamama riski mevcuttur.
>
> II. Müşteri Konsantrasyonu ve Kamçı Etkisi
> KLIC’in gelir yapısı son derece dikeydir. En büyük 10 müşteri (büyük OSAT'lar olan ASE, Amkor ve dev IDM'ler) toplam grup gelirlerinin %55'ini oluşturmaktadır.
>
> Risk: Son tüketici elektroniğindeki ani bir makroekonomik durgunluk, bu 10 dev firmanın CapEx bütçelerini anında dondurmasına yol açar. Arka uç üreticileri, tedarik zincirinin en sonunda yer aldığından "Kamçı Etkisi" nedeniyle sipariş iptallerini veya ertelemelerini en şiddetli hisseden grup olmaktadır.
>
> III. Jeopolitik Sıkışma ve Doğu Asya Riski
>
> KLIC her ne kadar Singapur merkezli ve ABD operasyonlu bir yapıya sahip olsa da en büyük yarı iletken montaj müşterileri ve dökümhaneleri Tayvan, Çin Halk Cumhuriyeti ve Güney Kore sınırları içerisindedir.
>
> Risk: ABD-Çin ticaret savaşlarının gelişmiş paketleme ekipmanlarına (özellikle TCB ve alt bileşenlerine) yönelik getirebileceği ek ihracat yasakları veya Tayvan Boğazı'ndaki olası bir lojistik aksama, şirketin backlog teslimatlarını tamamen felç edebilir.
>
> IV. CapEx ve Marj Baskısı
>
> Yıllık CapEx'in 12 milyon USD'den 22 milyon USD'ye çıkarılması, kısa vadede nakit akışını ve serbest nakit akışı marjlarını (Q2 FY2026'da düzeltilmiş serbest nakit akışı 6.3 milyon USD seviyesindedir) baskılamaktadır. Yeni hatların verimlilik oranlarında yaşanabilecek herhangi bir operasyonel aksaklık, Q3 ve Q4 brüt marj tahminlerini aşağı yönlü revize ettirebilir.
>
> 8. Stratejik Sonuç
>
> Kulicke & Soffa, döngüsel bir çöküşün ardından operasyonel karlılığa dönüş hikayesini başarıyla yazmıştır. Şirket, geleneksel iş kollarının sağladığı güçlü nakit akışını, geleceğin AI ve bellek standartları olan TCB, ProMEM ve dikey tel teknolojilerine başarıyla aktarmaktadır. Hisse senedinde son aylarda yaşanan güçlü momentum ve ralli, bu döngüsel dönüşün pazar tarafından satın alınmaya başladığını gösterse de FY2027 projeksiyonlarımız doğrultusunda şirketin çarpan büyümesinin henüz tamamlanmadığı değerlendirilmektedir. Bilançosunda borç bulunmayan, düzenli çeyreklik temettü ödeyen ve hisse geri alımlarıyla paydaş değerini destekleyen KLIC, uzun vadeli yarı iletken portföylerinde temel bir arka uç pozisyonu olarak öne çıkmaktadır.
>
> Yatırım tavsiyesi değildir.

### Kantique (@KantiqueTech)
_Sat Jul 11 19:03:01 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 18 · ↻ 5 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/KantiqueTech/status/2076019446376775983)

> 🚨Pendant la ruée vers l’or quantique, qui vend les pioches ?
>
> Si le calcul quantique explose, ce ne sont pas forcément les constructeurs de processeurs qui captureront toute la valeur. 
>
> Comme au XIXe siècle, les vrais gagnants pourraient être ceux qui fournissent les outils indispensables à tous.
>
> Les fournisseurs de l’ombre :
>
> •  Cryogénie : Oxford Instruments, Bluefors et Leiden Cryogenics dominent les réfrigérateurs à dilution qui refroidissent les systèmes supraconducteurs à quelques millikelvins. 
>
> Un goulot d’étranglement critique que personne ne peut contourner facilement.
>
> •  Lasers et photonique : TOPTICA       Photonics, M Squared Lasers, Coherent ($COHR ), Lumentum ($LITE ) et IPG Photonics fournissent les systèmes de précision nécessaires aux ions piégés et atomes neutres.
>
> •  Électronique de contrôle : FormFactor ($FORM ) et ses stations de test cryogéniques, ou MKS Instruments ($MKSI ), sont indispensables pour caractériser et faire fonctionner les puces quantiques.
>
> Ces entreprises vendent à toutes les modalités (supraconducteur, ion piégé, photonique, atome neutre). 
>
> Peu importe qui gagne la course aux qubits, elles restent essentielles.
>
> Dans la révolution quantique, les pioches et les pelles pourraient bien rapporter plus sûrement que l’or lui-même.
>
> Kantique — Le quantique décrypté.

### Melvin (@MelvinInvests)
_Sat Jul 11 19:35:17 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 93 · ↻ 30 · 💬 6 · [open on X](https://x.com/MelvinInvests/status/2076027568684401094)

> This is the supply chain that is running the entire AI revolution and here is how you can benefit from it (Save this). 
>
> When NVIDIA builds a GPU, the chip itself is only part of the story and those GPUs need to talk to each other at extraordinary speeds, across the same rack, across racks, across entire data centers. 
>
> The question of how data moves between chips is the defining bottleneck of the AI era and the answer is silicon photonics, moving data using light instead of copper wire.
>
> Think of copper as a country road and silicon photonics as a superhighway. 
>
> As AI clusters scale from one rack to hundreds of racks running millions of calculations simultaneously, copper runs out of bandwidth while light does not and here is you can benefit from this.
>
> Coherent ($COHR ) is the dominant supplier of optical transceivers and lasers inside every high-speed AI rack.  
>
> Their Q3 FY2026 revenue hit $1.81 billion, up 21% year over year with datacenter and communications now making up 72% of total revenue.  
>
> They are doubling their indium phosphide wafer capacity by end of year, a manufacturing advantage that produces four times the chips at less than half the cost of older technology.
>
> Marvell ($MRVL) spans both the copper switching layer and the silicon photonics layer through its Celestial AI acquisition, making it the most complete play across the entire networking stack.
>
> Corning ($GLW) is the fiber and every photon traveling between racks and between data centers travels through Corning's glass and they are expanding US fiber production by more than 50% and building three new manufacturing plants.
>
> Fabrinet ($FN) is the contract manufacturer that physically builds the optical modules for Coherent, Lumentum, and others.  
>
> Every time an optical company wins a new NVIDIA contract, Fabrinet's production volume goes up and it is a pure leverage on the entire sector without having to pick a winner between the component makers.
>
> IntelliEPI appears in both the SOI wafer layer and the light source layer of this supply chain, making them a double exposure name across two critical inputs.  
>
> When photonics capacity doubles, EPI wafer demand doubles first and almost no one tracks wafer substrate suppliers at this level.
>
> The thesis is simple as AI demand requires exponentially more data movement between chips, copper cannot keep up and light is the only solution. 
>
> Make sure to follow me @MelvinInvests for more overlooked opportunities in AI infrastructure.

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HM-GfHmXoAAD9sN.jpg

### Art of Speculation (@ArtofSpecuycky)
_Sat Jul 11 20:14:57 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 269 · ↻ 59 · 💬 42 · [open on X](https://x.com/ArtofSpecuycky/status/2076037548632363499)

> 光通信板块为什么跌这么惨？拆解Rosenblatt最新报告，聊聊我自己的判断
>
> 市场的担忧从哪来？
> 主要是三个因素叠加在一起：
> 一是市场担心中国厂商正在快速扩产磷化铟(InP)激光器产能， 害怕未来供给暴增导致价格战。
> 二是市场传出CPO(共封装光学)可能要推迟大约一年才能大规模部署， 这让不少人开始怀疑未来几年的光通信需求会不会跟着延后。
> 三是不少空头其实并不是真的看空这条赛道的基本面， 只是在借着这些消息和财报前的空窗期制造恐慌， 甚至有相当一部分空头计划在7月底、8月初财报公布前陆续回补空单， 部分人还打算2027年重新做多整个板块， 提前布局2028到2030年的CPO超级周期。
>
> 中国扩产到底是不是真正的威胁？
> 这是市场最关心的问题， 但我认为担心得有点过头了。 第一， 即便中国厂商持续扩产， 预计到2030年全球InP激光器的供给相比需求仍然存在大约40%的缺口， 行业整体依然缺货， 扩产短期内不会导致供给过剩。 
> 第二， 中国目前主要能量产的是低功率连续波激光器和100G EML， 应用场景集中在硅光收发器和800G模块这些相对成熟的产品线， 但真正未来几年最赚钱的200G EML和高功率连续波激光器， 中国还没有成熟的量产能力， 而这两样恰恰是CPO和NPO最核心的光源器件， 这意味着未来几年欧美厂商在高端环节依然握有明显的技术优势。 
> 第三， 中美供应链本身也在逐步脱钩， 出于政治因素、供应链安全、技术路线差异和客户认证体系不同这些原因， 欧美客户大概率不会转而采购中国厂商的产品， 目前Lumentum和Coherent很多产品已经排产到2027甚至2028年， 其中不少订单来自英伟达的提前锁单。
>
> CPO到底有没有真的延期？
> 我倾向于认为没有实质性延期。 
> CPO大致可以分两个阶段看：
> 第一阶段是小规模建设， 2026年下半年开始动工、2027年开始出货， 目前进度仍然按计划推进， 预计英伟达和博通2027年各自的产量都在3万到35万套左右。
> 第二阶段才是真正的大规模放量， 时间点在2028年。 而2027年这一年， NPO(近封装光学)会作为中间过渡方案承接一部分需求。
>
> 网络架构变化会不会减少光模块的需求？
> 市场还担心一件事，像MRC、RNG这类新的网络技术出现后， 会不会减少每台交换机需要的光模块数量。 确实有可能会从原来的6到7个下降到3到4个， 但GPU数量的增长速度远快于这个下降幅度， 整体光学需求预计仍然会持续增长， 这一点担心也偏多余。
>
> 几家公司的财报看点
> Lumentum这次财报压力相对最大， 因为它此前已经给出了市场上最激进的长期指引， 市场关注的是它能不能进一步上调2027年目标， 尤其是单季营收能不能达到20亿美元 (年化80亿美元)、营业利润率能不能超过40%。 Coherent这次是市场机构里比较偏爱的一家， 因为200G EML和高功率激光器的自产比例在持续提升， 加上刚拿到谷歌每年约10亿美元的1.6T模块订单， 以及英伟达2027到2030年的长期采购协议， 未来利润率有望持续改善。 
> AAOI这次财报可能会是营收和指引双双超预期的一份成绩单， 主要动力来自亚马逊和甲骨文的800G订单， 预计二季度收入能超过2亿美元、三季度指引接近3亿美元， 毛利率也会明显高于上半年大约30%的水平。 ANET的增长动力依然强劲， 主要客户覆盖Meta、微软、甲骨文、OpenAI、Anthropic、谷歌， 其中谷歌未来有可能成为它超过10%收入占比的大客户， 大量递延收入预计从2026年下半年开始确认， 带动下半年收入增速超过30%、2027年超过40%。
>
> 这份报告的核心结论
> 总结下来， 中国扩产确实是真实存在的现象， 但短期内不足以改变全球的供需格局。真正具备技术壁垒的200G EML、高功率激光器以及CPO相关产品， 欧美厂商依然领先。2028年仍然是CPO真正大规模放量的时间点， 2027年由NPO承接过渡需求。
> 目前光通信板块的这轮回调更多是情绪和预期驱动， 基本面没有恶化。即将到来的7月底到8月初财报季， 会是验证这条赛道需求是否依然强劲的重要窗口。
>
> 看完这份报告，我想补充一个自己的判断
> 我认为，短期缺货和未来出现结构性过剩并不矛盾（2026 2027年非常看好，2028年以后要注意），这两件事可以同时成立，关键要看过剩最先会出现在哪个环节。
>
> 现在整个行业都看到了AI需求，也都在积极扩产，云厂商也希望引入更多供应商来降低成本、分散供应链风险。如果未来800G、1.6T模块供应商越来越多，ASP下降速度开始快于成本下降速度，那么即使出货量和收入继续增长，毛利率也可能率先承压。
>
> 不过从目前来看，行业还远没有走到这一步。各家公司披露的信息依然指向供给紧张：高端激光器排产排到未来几年，积压订单维持高位，出口限制、良率、客户认证和测试能力仍然是主要瓶颈，真正缺的还是合格的高端产能。
>
> 如果未来行业进入供需再平衡，我认为最先面临价格压力的，大概率还是标准化程度较高的光模块环节，例如400G、逐渐成熟的800G，以及未来进入主流阶段的1.6T产品。像AAOI、中际旭创、新易盛、Source Photonics这类以光模块为主的厂商，未来更需要关注ASP和毛利率的变化。不过这是2028年以后更值得关注的风险，至少在我看来，2026至2027年行业仍然处于供不应求阶段，AAOI等公司依然受益于订单释放、产能爬坡和业绩兑现。
>
> 相比之下，我更看好拥有核心器件壁垒的高端零部件公司，例如Lumentum（LITE）、Coherent（COHR）；以及Ciena（CIEN）、Nokia（NOK）等系统层公司，它们更多依靠技术、网络架构和系统集成能力竞争。至于Veeco（VECO）、Aehr（AEHR）、Viavi（VIAV）等设备和测试公司，只要行业仍在扩产，就有望持续受益于资本开支周期。
>
> 时间线上，我的判断和这份报告基本一致：2026年至2027年上半年仍是供不应求；2027年下半年至2028年，随着新增产能逐步释放，市场会开始重新定价供需关系。
>
> 现在讨论整个光通信行业全面产能过剩还为时过早。未来几年，不同产品、不同技术路线和不同公司，大概率会进入完全不同的供需周期，不会整个行业一起过剩。

>
> > Slow Recovery: Mobile represented over half of Soitec's FY26 revenue. Price hikes by smartphone manufacturers are creating downside risks to consensus projections.
>

### revoAIution (@revoAIution)
_Sat Jul 11 23:15:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 40 · ↻ 1 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/revoAIution/status/2076082860138602895)

> Goldman Sachs April 2026 report projects Silicon Photonics growing from 6 percent of the datacom market today to 45 percent by 2028.
>
> Most people read that as a threat to laser companies.
> It is actually the opposite for $SIVE.
>
> Silicon is great at moving light around. But it cannot create light. That is just physics. You always need an external laser feeding light into a Silicon Photonics chip.
> That external laser is what $SIVE makes.
>
> As Silicon Photonics grows from 6 to 45 percent of the market the demand for external CW lasers grows right alongside it.
>
> Goldman basically proved the opposite of what most people assume. More Silicon Photonics means more laser demand. Not less.
